OMG Jen - Thank you so much.  This review is from a person who had to go outside when my mom or anyone cooked cabbage!  Could not stand the smell.  This recipe is great. The only thing I did different and proably everyone else knew to do this - but I have never, ever cooked cabbage - I did add salt and pepper and covered it to help wilt the cabbage faster.  Not for too long and when thoroughly cooked, it was still a little crisp and delicious.  I loved it and my family did as well. I am 67 y/o and considered to be a good cook in my circle, but this recipe absolutely tops all of mine.  Thank you so very much.  A fan!

text:
I am not sure what those who gave the recipe "mediocre" or bad ratings were expecting. As one can see, it is a very simple recipe with a very simple result. I would not omit the vinegar, as in such a small amount compared to the volume of cabbage, i dont feel that it could be offensive. but i do think it adds a subtle and important flavor. I also suggest increasing the amount of bacon to your taste. I mean, its bacon, so the more the merrier. i used 5 slices. also, this is one of those dishes that makes for leftovers that get better and better.

This is one of my favorite comfort foods.  I make mine a little different though.  I always add about 3 potatoes, and some crushed red pepper.  Sometimes adding either or both ham (instead of bacon) and mushrooms.  It makes it more of a complete meal.  I never add vinegar or sugar.  Pile it all in the pan and add about a cup of water put the cover on and let it simmer down till all the water is gone and the potatoes are done.  I like it all mashed up together in my bowl with butter!!!!

text:
This is a wonderful and easy recipe. This is only the second time I made cabbage. The first time I made it was horrible. This is like the traditional southern cabbage we have here. I followed the recipe with a few exceptions. #1. I used three large cloves of garlic, #2 I used more onions (because I love onions and garlic, #3. I used it in an iron cast dutch oven and did not need ANY water, #4. The best tip you can get about bacon grease...use it to sautee your stuff but then use a little more at the very end to add the flavor in since the onions and garlic absorb a lot of the bacon grease flavor, and I also crumbled the bacon on top of the cabbage instead of mixing it in the cabbage. It was wonderful. Thank you!

text:
This is pretty much how I remember my grandmother making her fried cabbage. The cabbage came from her garden, and she would use a half a pound of real thick sliced bacon because she was feeding a lot of people usually. She would cut the bacon into "lardons", and when it was cooked crisp, take it out and put it aside and then cook the cabbage, salt, pepper and only a teaspoon of sugar until the cabbage was carmelized in areas and soft and fragrant. She would put it all in a serving bowl, add the bacon back in, mix it with a serving spoon, and put the vinegar cruet right next to it on the table. Amazing! She has been gone many years, but every time I see this recipe I think of her.

text:
We love cabbage with bacon. I use pre-cooked bacon to lessen the clean up and saturated fat. I Cook it in the microwave, I use 1 slice of bacon to each cup of cabbage.I never add sugar I add grated Apple instead, a sweet apple with or without the skin.To make this go faster I cook the chopped onion (I use a whole onion)in the microwave in a little oil, about Five minutes till it is translucent then transfer it to my wok pan. I wilt the cabbage in the microwave it becomes a nice bright green. Then add apple and cabbage to wok pan. When cabbage is tender to your liking sprinkle with Cider vinegar and crumbled bacon. This is always a hit.

This has been a family favorite since I was a little girl! Love this recipe! It is definitely a "fly by the seat of your pants" recipe...throw in more 
bacon, a little more onion...it's up to you! I even make a version where I use sliced keilbasa and add cooked egg noodles at the end to make a meal of it. 
To the reviewer that used bagged shredded cabbage - I don't recommend using it, and that is probably why you didn't enjoy the recipe. I've tried that in the past, and the shred is too fine. You need  larger pieces of cabbage - the finely shredded cabbage in the bag wilts way too much.

Disappointed in this one.  Then again, maybe I'm just not a fried cabbage fan.  My biggest issue with this recipe is the way it's written.  First of all the ingredients call for 6 cups of cabbage and then instructs you to cut it into wedges.  How much is 6 cups?  A weight measurement would have been more helpful.  Another problem I found is the recipe never indicates that you cover your skillet while cooking for 15 minutes.  In that amount of time, at medium high heat, the 2 T. of water would have been long gone!  Poorly written and far too vague.  It's no wonder my outcome was poor.

country:

text:
My Bavarian Mother used to make this all the time when I was growing up. I didn't care much for it when I was younger, but grew fond of it later as my taste buds matured.  I made it exactly according to the recipe the first time, and it was exquisite.  I tend to be an experimental cook, and can't leave well enough alone, so I altered it a bit since then....  I toasted 2 cups of pecans (with butter in baking pan @ 350 for 7-10 mins), let cool, then chopped.  After removing the bacon, I added 2 cups of peeled & deveined fresh meduim shrimp to the bacon grease, cooked until pink. Removed them, and set them aside with the bacon. After step 2, I stirred in the shrimp and toasted pecans pieces to the final mix. It comes out excellent every time.

text:
I made this recipe this evenng.  We had a pound bag of coleslaw from the grocers (w/o the dressing). I used balsalmic vinegar, made the dish a rather dark color.  I used about two Tbs. of b. vinegar, several pinches of sugar and three thick slices of bacon.  Removed the bacon and some grease and then topped it with the latter at the end.  
This recipe was good and I will make it again.  The three of us ate it all.  However, I don't think it's "the best".  I think cabbage is sort of hard to make "delicious".
I would recommend more vinegar for a sweet and sour taste.  Bacon didn't add that much to the dish. It vaguley reminded me of German potato salad.

I made this yesterday for a get together with a bunch of guys drinking beer & BBQing stuff.  I made it at my house, put it into a large Pyrex casserole dish for transport.  My sampling at home told me it would be well received (otherwise I would have left it at home and went over empty handed).  What I didnt' expect....is that warming it up in the oven once at my destination....made it BETTER!!  It got crispy around the edges and the bacon got crispy again as well.

The guys loved it and next time, I'm going to put it into the oven to get it all really crispy.  I think that's the little kick it needed to make it 5 stars.

Thanks Jen for the recipe.  It was really good & I look forward to playing with this recipe.  Also next time I'm going to use 1/2 head of green cabbage & 1/2 of red for a visual change.

I'll report back.

I enjoyed this recipe so much!  I love cabbage, and right now it is very inexpensive, because of St. Patrick's Day, so I bought a lot of cabbage this week. text:
This will be my new go-to cabbage recipe!  I used a sub-par brand of bacon, so that part was a little chewy, but this dish still turned out excellent.  My Irish grandma always doused her boiled cabbage in cider vinegar, so that seemed normal to me!  And I cannot bring myself to leave the cider vinegar out....it enhances the flavor so much.  A nice - and unexpected - side effect of frying vs. boiling...it had almost no impact on my stomach.  Often boiled cabbage can come back to haunt the household (if you get my drift!), but I had none of that.  I'm the only one in my home that will eat cabbage, so I had plenty for leftovers and it was just as good warmed up as fresh.  Thanks!

Excellent meal!  I used five strips of bacon because that's what I had left in the package but otherwise followed the recipe.  I tasted it prior to adding the apple cider vinegar and it was cabbage fried in bacon fat:  decent but, you know. text:
Been making fried cabbage since I was a kid,  but no sugar, vinegar or any of the other stuff. Just fry the chopped up bacon until crispy, remove and drain on paper towel leaving bacon grease in skillet, add roughly chopped cabbage on medium high  heat , stirring occasionally until tender crisp, then add bacon back in stirring to mix. Salt and pepper to taste.  Two ingredients,  easy-peasy.

text:
This turned out pretty good. I didn't measure the cabbage, just cooked up the whole head that I had, so I had to adjust the ingredients accordingly. I omitted the sugar since I'm on a low carb diet and had to double the vinegar as I couldn't taste a difference with just one tablespoon. I also used a whole pound of bacon and reserved 1/4 cup of the grease, half of which was used to cook the onion and the other half added when the cabbage went in. A very tasty dish, and a great way to use up cabbage. I certainly wouldn't call it mediocre, and probably not awesome, but good? Definitely, yes.

text:
I love the ease of preparation of this recipe. My family really loved the the flavor. Even my son (who hates cabbage) gave it 3 stars. The vinegar was the added extra touch to this easy, flavorful dish. 

As with ANY cabbage dish, DO NOT OVER COOK the cabbage, and DO NOT USE ALUMINUM PANS. 
Cabbage contains isothiocynates that break down into smelly sulfur compounds during cooking. The reaction is even stronger in aluminum pans. The longer the cabbage is cooked the more smelly the compounds become. The solution; a brief cooking time. Cook just until tender and use stainless steel pots and pans.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
If you don't want tasteless boiled cabbage, try this recipe. Followed Step 1 and 1st line of step 2, however, instead of cooking cabbage with onions & bacon grease, I drizzled a generous spoon of drippings over chopped cabbage in separate large pot. Sauteed it for 10 minutes (be careful not to scorch). I then mixed in onions and added tsp of brn sugar, S&P, good splash of white balsamic vinegar & 1/4 tsp of liquid smoke. I transfered to a ovenproof ceramic dish, covered & set to the side. I was roasting a corned beef in a 325 oven so I prepared this recipe early afternoon to finish in oven during last 1/2 hour. I tossed with the pre-cooked bacon pieces + 1 more dash of vinegar immediately after removing from oven. Good recipe you can prepare in-advance this way. Turned out tender but with texture. Even better next day (lightly fried).
